text:
Perfect for a late night chocolate craving and an urge to bake as they go into and out of the oven quickly. In my hurry, however, I didn't bother to read any of the reviews before I started and wish I had. I would have learned that other than using oil instead of butter, this is the same recipe as "Best Brownies," also from this site. (I happen to love that recipe!)  In that recipe, however, an 8x8" pan is used.  No wonder these turned out so thin, as others have noted! I used the 9x9" pan this recipe called for and while I was pleased with the brownie itself, which was moist, fudgey, with a bit of a crispy edge, I was disappointed in how thin they turned out. Unfortunately, that was a deal breaker for me as it made for a rather unimpressive looking brownie. Also, I found 18 minutes baking time perfect, so it's no wonder others found these dry if they were baking them for the recommended 20-25 minutes! Good brownie ingredients-wise, but somewhat flawed directions in terms of both pan size and baking time.

text:
This is the recipe I've been using to bake brownies for well over a decade now, even before I attended culinary school!  I notice the latest reviewer complained about the gritty taste of the sugar in the product.  I suggest she try either butter or if she wants to cut out butterfat in her diet, use a 1/4 cup of butter and make the rest vegetable oil, or stick to all vegetable oil, but do the following anyway:  Microwave it for 1-2 minutes or until it melts(or oil is warmed).  Add the sugar to the warm/hot butter/oil, and this melts the sugar.  Better yet, try honey! I've also taken out as much as a half cup of sugar out of the recipe, and it works fine.  Microwaving or heating the oil causes the sugar to melt slightly, and if she uses a wire whisk to mix, it can also help to blend the butter, sugar and eggs together more smoothly.  Don't ever give up on a recipe after one try, because it's not a fair assessment of it.  Anything can cause a recipe to "fail" (the temps outside, the oven too hot/cool, not familiar with the recipe) in the first try.  I urge her to try again, and maybe try some of my tips.

O M G...These are by far the best brownies I have ever had in my short 38 years!!!! I, however, had no 9x9 pan. I used my glass 8x8 baking dish, added 1/4 cup milk chocolate chips mixed into batter, and did use another reviewer's suggestion of melted butter instead of vegetable oil. 
Also, since my pan was 8x8, I knew they would be a little thicker than the 9x9 would produce so I increased the baking time to 30 minutes exactly. OMG, I swear by this recipe and I've tried many homemade ones and ALL boxed versions. If you haven't tried this, do yourself a favor especially now around Valentine's Day....TRY THIS RECIPE!! Thank you thank you thank you to Sarah who gave us this DEELISH homemade brownie recipe! (My 4 yr old thanks you too!)

text:
These were wonderful! Very very close to being as good as one of the better boxed mixes! I used an 8x8 pan, added 2 tbls of chocolate syrup and a handful of chocolate chips, used melted butter instead of the oil as some of the other reviewers had done. I ended up baking for almost 30 minutes. Do NOT over bake! Be sure to remove these when a toothpick inserted in the center comes out with moist crumbs clinging to it, and  NOT getting to the point where the toothpick would come out completely clean. You will have a super fudgy, moist brownie. I wish it was a tad bit more chewy, but wouldn't mess with the recipe because it really is SO good and SUPER easy.  It is nice and chocolatey so I don't think I really needed to add the chocolate chips. Thanks for the recipe! YUM!

text:
This is my first review on this site.  I have never before felt a need to add my views.  

These brownies will work if you need a late night pick me up, or a quick baked good, but the flavor is lacking.  

I made this 3 times, once with olive oil(didn't like), once with butter(didn't like), and then I tried adding some mini morsels.  Even after all of that the texture and flavor just was not what I expect from a brownie.  

I used an 8x8 pan and I am very glad I did because they were very thin.  I did not add any additional time.  

They were not gooey, but more cake like.  All 3 times I had allowed my eggs to reach room temperature prior to using them.  

The other problem I had is they are very bland, and lack that rich chocolate flavor.  Even with the help of the chocolate chips I still did not get that gooey moist brownie flavor I love in a brownie.

I am at this point moving on because if I modify this further I might as well write a new recipe myself.

I didn't think anything could be better than Ghirardelli box brownies, but these really are so much better! My boyfriend was impressed. Took the advice of other reviewers and subbed melted butter for the oil and that made them taste extra rich. Also added a handful of choco chips. There's another recipe on here, "Best Brownies", that is identical to this one except it has frosting - based on how these taste, I'd say frosting would be gilding the lily. These brownies come out rich, chocolately, and chewy, and the only thing I would change next time is to make a double batch! Thanks, Sarah, for a great recipe I'll make again and again.

These were good and better the next day.  I added a handful of bittersweet chocolate chips to the mixture and a handful of caramel chips.  I also used melted butter instead of oil and added extra vanilla.  They did turn out a bit thin in the 9x9 pan so if you like your brownies thicker, use a 8x8. text:
These are very moist, tasty brownies.  Instead of using oil, I used 1/4 cup of melted butter, and then 1/4 cup of pumpkin puree. No one noticed, because the butter gave the brownies a richer flavor. I skipped the nuts (they were for my little brother's birthday...he requested chocolate brownies with no nuts, just chocolate chips!) and added 1/3 cup of mini chocolate chips instead. The only problem I had with this is that I made it in the specified 9x9" square pan, and they were too thin. I will use an 8x8" pan next time I make these. My brother wanted frosting, so I used half a recipe of Texas Chocolate Frosting (from this site) on these and it was perfect. Thanks for sharing...these are great!!!

text:
If you're looking for a rich, chocolatey, melt in your mouth type brownies, these are not it. This recipe is just ok, not fabulous. I'm not quite sure why it has such high reviews. I tried this recipe twice before revewing and folowed it exactly as listed. The first time I used melted butter as recommended, the second time I used the oil in the original recipe. Both times I found the brownies to be more sticky and sweet with a sugary, oily aftertaste rather than rich and chocolately, which is how I prefer them. Brownies aren't very hard to make and there aren't many ingredients so I have a hard time giving a 5 star rating for a simple overly sweet recipe when to me it tasted exactly like something I could have gotten out of a box and spent half the time preparing. I think a recipe with more chocolate and less sugar and one which allows for a thicker, richer, more chocolatey outcome is what I was looking for.

text:
These brownies are fantastic!  I did make them with melted butter instead of oil because I wanted the extra richness.  That definitely did it!  I have to agree with some other reviewers that said they were too greasy.  I'll probably skip greasing the pan next time.  However, once cooled, I placed a plate on top of the pan and turned the brownies out, upside down.  I then covered the now exposed bottom with 2 paper towels and carefully flipped them back over.  The paper towels soaked upmall the extra grease and then they were TO DIE FOR!  Wonderful!

text:
OMG!!  These are the best brownies!!  Before now, I have thought that the best recipe was from either my "Aunt Betty" or "Uncle Duncan", but these are just as good, and healthier because I recognize all of the ingredients!  Made exactly like the recipe, but with butter and added 1/3 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips (no nuts).  I used very good cocoa.  Out of this world!  Tips:  grease pan VERY well.  DO NOT OVERMIX (just like the ones in the box).  Let cool completely and cut with a plastic knife (works every time).  I cooked them about 22 1/2 minutes--take out when they are a bit crisp around the edges, but not pulling completely away.  (the toothpick test does NOT work on brownies).  They will be perfect!

text:
Made these the other day and YES, these are mmm-mmm better (BEST) brownies!  It was so easy to make them and they are simply scrumptious.  I did not use a mixer, I simply stirred the ingredients. I used melted butter rather than vegetable oil and did not add nuts. I made them in an 8x8 pan and cut them into small squares.  I wouldn't change anything. Interestingly, this recipe is the same as Absolutely Best Brownies (from this site) if you use regular flour rather than self-rising (as submitter suggests if you want less cake-like brownies). Then today I saw a recipe called Best Brownies (again, AR), also identical recipe.  That one includes directions for frosting. I might use frosting but honestly does not need it. Proof they're truly the best brownies -- everyone everywhere is submitting the recipe and getting 5 stars all over the place.  You won't be disappointed in this recipe!  Thanks for submitting.

So, I have just recently started baking (you have to be so precise) and decided to try this recipe.  This is the best brownie (aside from my mom's) that I have ever tasted.  I made a double batch, so I used applesauce, whole wheat flour and choc. chips.  I also used grape seed oil, instead of veg oil (I never buy that stuff); mixed all together and put in a 9x13 pan lined with parchment paper and lightly sprayed the bottom; baked for approx 25 min, turned off oven and let sit for another 5-10 minutes.  These surprised me by coming out fantastic, since I don't usually bake (I have a chef's stove and do great at just cooking, you don't have to measure).  I would highly recommend these.

text:
I always wondered what "from-scratch" brownies would taste like, and since making these I've decided there's no reason to go back to boxed mixes! What I love about this recipe is that it is cocoa-powder-based instead of melted-chocolate-based, so if you don't have a huge amount of chocolate chips on hand, you can still throw together some brownies. The recipe turns out great as-is, but I like to make a few small modifications to make it even better. I usually add about 1/3 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips to the batter, which enhances the dark chocolate flavor - getting little pieces of chocolate in your brownie definitely heightens the YUM factor. I usually substitute light brown sugar for half of the white sugar. I've also added about 1/3 cup walnuts, substituted half of the oil with applesauce, substituted the oil with melted butter, and added instant espresso powder - it always turns out nicely. Give this recipe a try, and you can impress people by claiming that you even make *brownies* from scratch! :)

I am of the opinion that "home-cooked" and "from scratch" baking recipes should be better than anything from a box.  These were good, but just shy of amazing.  In all honesty you can find a better brownie from a Ghiradelli box (which sets a fairly high standard). This recipe is perfect as is! I have a "crew" of college age boys (my grandson and his friends) who love it! The only change I have to make is to double the recipe to feed them all. 
Sometimes I add different flavorings to the recipe, a bit of coconut extract or orange oil in addition to the vanilla. Today I made a chocolate-orange ganache for the top. I plan to garnish with freshly grated orange zest. 
But make no mistake, these brownies don't need anything; they are wonderful made exactly as the recipe directs. Thank you, Sarah!

text:
These are very yummy :) I have three hungry little boys and these brownies don't last long! Okay the first time I made them exactly like the recipe except for the walnuts because we don't really like nuts in brownies and they were yummy but they were kind of missing a savory element. The second time I used 1/4 cup margarine 1/4 cup vegetable oil and they were a little bit better but still wanted a little more richness. I just made them tonight for dessert and used all butter and they're delish!! Sweet, fudgy and just enough savory richness, mmmm......so with using butter instead of vegetable oil I give these brownies five stars using oil more like four but still very good!

Love these! I don't make brownies often enough, but I recently needed to make a lactose-free dessert for a friend and these are splendid! Super moist ad just sweet enough without being dense-wet like super-sweet store-bought desserts. I also through in a handful of coarsely grounded black sesame powder since I had some on hand (& to go with another dessert I was making) and it took it to another level. It's very subtle, so it's not earth shattering, but it adds fiber & when you bite into it, you go, "Oh, look at that. That's interesting".

text:
i was looking for a cocoa-based brownie made with oil - a pantry recipe.  These are excellent, nicely fudgy and zero fuss.    Used Hershey's Special Dark cocoa powder, sifted the dry ingredients together, and baked in an 8 x 8 pan.  To ensure moist brownies, mix just until the dry ingredients are blended, and bake until just barely done.   This is a keeper!

I had no butter in the house and needed something sweet, quick and delicious to take to a birthday party. These did the trick.  They were simple to make in a pinch. I thought the oil may overpower the taste in the finished product, but no. They were delicious and were an big hit!  I wish I had doubled the recipe as they were gone almost instantly.  I gave 4 stars.. as personally, I would prefer a bit more chocolatey taste.  These had a nice subtle chocolate flavor.  I added a bit more vanilla and did not add walnuts...Also, as a note,  I thought they were going to be a flop when I took them out of the oven as they flattened in the pan.  Shrinking aside, they came out tasty and delicious! I will definitely make again... and again :)

text:
These are the best and easiest brownies!  I have been making these brownies for years and will not try another.  No melting butter!  No melting chocolate!  I like to mix regular cocoa with Dutch-processed cocoa which gives the brownies a little richer chocolatiness and darker color.  Don't waste your time and effort - double the recipe and bake in a 9x13!  To get that exta crackly top layer - beat the eggs and sugar first until pale in color and light and fluffy - about 5 minutes.  Or skip this step and make as directed.  Either way it's a win-win!

The top wasn't very pretty--it doesn't have the glossy sheen you can get from other brownies, but they make up for it in taste! I used a peanut butter frosting recipe from here (from the brownies with peanut butter frosting recipe) and added some chopped butterfinger, neither of which were necessary except I wanted to jazz them up for work. They didn't cut particularly cleanly, but who cares... they are fudgy and yummy!

I wish I could give this recipe even more stars! I've made it twice and will never use another from-scratch recipe again. No more boxed mixes in my house. Ever. Seriously. They are gooey in the extreme (Note: I doubled the recipe both times) but I think an extra egg would help them stay firmer, because I'm using large rather than extra large eggs. No complaints, just a tip. Also, the second time I made this recipe, I doubled it and added about 3/4 cup fresh strawberries, diced and dredged in flour. Next time, trying more (1 - 1.5 cups) of strawberries and/or raspberries. I can't wait to do it again, but my waistline can :)

text:
Very pleasing brownie recipe!  It is so easy to throw together and has ingredients that most everybody has on-hand at any given time.  It's nice to be able to use vegetable oil instead of using up a stick of butter from your fridge and/or waiting for one to soften to room temp.  Check them early at about 18-19 minutes if you're like me and like your brownies on the fudgy side as opposed to cakey.  If they're still runny, just keep checking them every 2-3 minutes thereafter.    Followed the recipe to the letter, except for the vanilla.  I didn't have any, so I put teaspoon-size squirt (judging with my eye) of maple syrup.  I have no idea if that made any difference whatsoever, but it won't hurt anything.  ;-)

text:
Definitely a favorite in our house! We always double the recipe and bake in a 9x13 pan. Using melted butter instead of vegetable oil is a must. It makes the brownies ten times better. It's a great recipe to try different things with. We sometimes put white or semisweet chocolate chips in the mix. We have also been known to pour half of the mix in the pan, then pour a layer of melted caramel in the middle, then the rest of the brownie mix. Bake it at the same temperature for the same amount of time. It turns out perfect every time.

text:
I was craving chocolate one night and found this recipe. It was very easy and oh so delicious! 

I used 1/2 of butter instead of oil and melted it in the microwave and then added it to the sugar to dissolve it a little. I added mini marshmallows to the mix. I also melted PB and swirled it on the top before I put the pan in the oven. It turned out great because I love PB and chocolate together and the marshmallows gave it a nice gooey texture.
 
The next time I make these, I will swirl raspberry jam instead of PB. Giada De Laurentiis did it on her show on the Food Network and it looked so good. The possibilities are endless!

Wow! These are some amazingly good brownies! I tossed 1/2 cup of chocolate chips in a tsp of cocoa powder and folded them into the batter before baking. An excellent recipe!

Edited 8/18/2012 - I think I just made an even better version!  After mixing, and before adding the choc chips, I reserved 2/3 cup of batter. When the rest of it was in the pan, I mixed 1/2 cup of hazelnut cocoa spread (Nutella or Jiff type) and 2 tbs of very strong coffee. Then, I spooned it over the top of the rest of the batter and swirled it before baking. SO good!

UPDATE:Used half white sugar and brown sugar, used white wheat flour, added 1 Tbl corn syrup and 1/2 cup choc chips instead of nuts. Left out the baking powder. Baked for 20 min @ 350.  Awesome brownies!

I just made these and followed the recipe exactly (didn't add nuts) and added 1/2 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips.  I have been on a brownie rampage to find a good homemade recipe that resembles the box brownies.  I have made 3 different brownie recipes within the last 2 days, and these are exactly what i have looking for!  The taste is just like the boxed version and the cocoa powder doesn't overpower the finished product.  Mine did have to cook longer, closer to 35 minutes on 350 degrees F.  I baked them in a clear 1 1/2 quart baking dish and was able to get 16 pieces.  I think I like my brownies baked with oil.  I noticed when I use butter, they come out more cake-like....?  I am not a big fan of cake-like brownies.  So, these seem to be what I have been looking for in a homemade brownie!  I'm so happy!********Update: I used 1/2 cup melted butter and a packet of Carnation (Breakfast Esstentials) and about 2/3 cup of sugar, next time use 1/2 cup if usinf the carnation packet(instead of 1 cup). Then followed the rest of the ingredients, except nuts.  Used a 9x9, baked at 350F for 20 -25 min and they were very moist, but didn't have the shiny, cracked top.  So, I used half of the Easy Chocolate Bundt Cake Glaze By: TUNISIANSWIFE, from this site.  They are so yummy!

text:
These were phenomenal. I didn't even prepare them quite right, and they turned out well, though definitely not brownie-like - my own fault. I didn't have all-purpose flour, so I used 1/4c of self-rising, and they didn't turn out one bit cakelike. I didn't add the baking soda or salt, either. Butter was subbed for veg. oil, badly melted, and I mixed the cocoa in before I was supposed to, but that didn't seem to make a difference aside from a little lumps in the batter. No butter spray, used olive oil instead. I don't know if that's what resulted in a bunch of gooey residue on the bottom or what, since i hardly used more than half a teaspoon, but either way, it didn't affect the taste. I underbaked a little, so they were definitely not solid enough to hold, but i made do with a fork. If I were to go back and redo this correctly, I'm sure they'd turn out even better!

This recipe is FANTASTIC! I just made them tonight after finding this recipe online. For just a few basic ingredients, these brownies came out so delicious. The only thing I had to change was the cooking time. I had to let it bake more like 35 min.  In a nut shell, this recipe is a keeper. ;-)  **UPDATE: I had to come back and change my stars to 5. I'm giving these 3 stars, but the recipe is probably worthy of 4 stars.  It was a quick & easy recipe to satisfy the sweet tooth of a self-proclaimed chocolate lover (my husband).  But, my personal preference for a different texture than this recipe produces largely contributed to the rating.  While moist and fudgy inside, the brownies were a little crunchy on the outside.  I prefer a more "cakey" texture.  The flavor is quite good and I mixed a handful of semi-sweet chocolate chips into the batter before spreading into the pan to bake, which was a nice addition to the "chocolatyness". Would probably make these again, but they wouldn't be my go-to brownie recipe.

As reviewer  MELLO 57 noticed, these ARE the same as "best brownies" recipe from this site, except that the other one asks for butter instead of oil. I tried it both ways and both are really good. I make it with oil when I feel lazy or in a hurry because it is easier and faster! This is a really delicious chewy and chocolatey brownie made either way. I do recommend adding some chocolate chips to the batter and on top as it makes it so much more decadent and delicious!

text:
Reliable brownie recipe, made twice and came out great each time. Next time I will double the recipe, as it doesn't make 16 brownies, more like 6. I did make some chances to lower the calories - used 1/4 butter, melted, and mixed in 1/4 cup of plain lowfat yogurt or unsweetened applesauce, and used this combo instead of oil. I also used 18 packets of Splenda instead of the 1 cup of sugar, since I don't like overly sweet brownies. Each time mine came out more cake-y than chewy, but still delicious. Maybe not the best in the world, but pretty good and simple and easy to lighten up by substituting the oil and sugar for low-cal equivalents.

text:
YUUUMMY!!! Do not listen to others who claim these are dry. A dry brownie means it was over cooked.  Not all ovens are the same and an oven thermometer is a great investment to make sure you are always at the right temp. This recipe produced a very moist and chewy brownie for me and even the edges were moist but perfectly baked. I only added a squirt of Hershey's chocolate syrup and 1/3 cup of semi-sweet chocolate chips to the mix before baking. The only reason I give this recipe 4 stars instead of 5 is because it did leave a slight after taste.  I'm not sure if it was because of the oil.  Will definitely try again with melted unsalted butter.  DELISH!

text:
It looks like someone may have copied this recipe and re-listed it as the "Absolutely Best Brownies," which also has a rating of nearly 5 stars. Since I saw & tried this recipe first, I'm giving it the 5 stars. These brownies are a tad sweet for me, so I like to cut the sugar by 1/4 cup, but my boyfriend raved about them. I found through experimentation that adding ground golden flaxseed meal during the dry phase or after the batter is mixed (and before the walnuts are added) gives the brownies a slightly different texture and flavor that really compliments them, especially with the walnuts since the meal is itself subtly nutty. I've made this recipe several times now and can say it's results are addictive. Love 'em. I tend to kick up the cocoa content a little more for its antioxidants, but I'm sure that messes with the ratios. Anyway, as my bf says, "these are the best brownies I have ever eaten."

These were very easy to make I followed the recipe exactly with the walnuts, but made a double batch in a 9x13 pan baked for 35-38 min. Then I added about 2 tbsp of softened butter. I also added marshmallows about 1 cup and frozen Nutella cubes which added wonderful pockets of Nutella ( about 10 tsp of Nutella. Freeze them on wax paper &  chop in half. Put half of the cubes in the batter mix & the other half on top right before they go into the oven.) they basically turned into rocky road brownies.

Followed the recipe to a T. They are very cakey, no fudgy-ness to them at all but there is a bit of moisture so it's not totally bone dry at least. I am not overly fond of the taste and would not say this produces better results than a boxed mix (which is what I was looking for). There was not a nice flake on top that you often see and really just looks and tastes like a chocolate cake. The creator does recommend using butter instead of oil for a rich and buttery taste, so perhaps that may amend this. Seems safe to say if you do not want cake-y brownies, try it with butter.

text:
Really good brownies! Great for a late night craving. I had all the ingredients on hand,  which I think the average home baker would. The only changes I made was to add 1/4 teaspoon of instant coffee, and use a mix of cake flour and all purpose flour. I pretty much always add the equivalent of  however much salt the recipe calls for in instant coffee (so 1/4 teaspoon of salt and 1/4 teaspoon of instant coffee)  to any chocolate recipe to enhance the chocolate flavor. I didn't have quite a half cup of all purpose flour,  so I added  a couple of tablespoons of cake flour to make the half cup called for. 

This is a fudge type brownie that begs for ice cream on top. Even with the little bit of cake flour added,  these were still fudgy. If you prefer a cake like brownie,  I don't recommend this recipe. 

I agree with another reviewer that said they're kind of thin.  I didn't mind,  it just gave me an excuse to eat more! But just keep that in mind. Probably and 8x8 pan would be better.  Or maybe even a mini muffin pan. These would make awesome brownie bites! Just reduce the baking time. 

All in all, a solid fudge type brownie. Emergency sweet tooth satisfied!

text:
(Semi Important Note. I added 1/2 cup of melted butter in place of the oil. It suggests this in the description) 
     This is the best brownie recipe that I have found in my years of baking, period. It is soft, fudgy, and it melts in your mouth wonderfully! One of the greatest parts about it is that it can sit over-night without becoming hard.  A lot of brownies that I have made in the past have done this so I was very pleased when this did not happen to this one. I highly suggest it for casual dinners when you want an easy from scratch desert without going to the trouble of a more advanced recipe. 
     There are two things in the making of this brownie that I suggest you do not do.
     (1) Do not over-bake this! It will become hard and dry if you do. Take it out of the oven when the edges start to pull away from the pan (it says this in the recipe). It will wiggle in the middle and there is a good chance that a toothpick inserted in the center will come out with some batter on it. This is okay, it will solidify while sitting.
     (2) Do not over mix this. If you do than the batter will be filled with air bubbles and it will be more cake-like.

     Overall, this recipe is fantastic and I highly suggest it!

country:
None
text:
My recipes are packed away and we were looking for a similar recipe of my mother's that I grew up making...and I have made for over 45 years.  This is VERY close....though I do nto remember any baking powder in hers.   After making them I looked at some of the low star reviews... and feel the need to make a few comments.   Cake like:  skip the baking powder.  Oily/basking in oil:  ???? did not happen to me and never has.  Not rich enough: add a little more cocoa and/or add a pinch of instant coffee granules.   Prefer the box mix: Stick with your processed fast foods.
 Also, for brownies...do not over mix.   I only use a spoon to mix.  Blend oil/sugar/vanilla enough to be incorporated.  Add the eggs and again blend only enough to well incorporate.  Do the same with the dry.  As for cooking times... it will depend on your oven and the type of pan you use.    I did 4 stars only because I feel the baking powder can be skipped.

text:
I've made these brownies 3x this week and finally figured out how to get the brownie that I want. 

The changes I made were:

-beat eggs and sugar for a few minutes until pale yellow and thick. Do this first before adding the remaining ingredients. This creates a nice crust on top of brownies.

-Use butter instead of oil for more flavor

-I added 1 tsp of instant coffee granules to give brownies oomp 

-Use 8x8 pan lined with parchment paper and reduced the baking time.

These came out pretty okay. They were nicely goey inside with a good texture. However,  I think due to the amount of sugar and mixed with the oil it made the top brownie layer a little too sugarary crispy. Even in a 8x8" pan it was rather thin so next time I will use 1.5 times the recipe for a thicker brownie and perhaps use all butter to see if it's better. My top had little air bubbles from the baking powder but the next day it looked better with a bit of a shiny crackled top.

text:
These are really GOOD!!! Don't get me wrong, this is a really good recipe. The brownies were really chewy and very chocolatey. This is my first time using this recipe and they were a complete success!! My family loved them. I usually use a different recipe that requires chocolate chips, but I didn't have any at that time, so I looked for a substitute and these are great! This recipe is definitely a keeper. When I don't have chocolate chips, I'll make these, when I do I'll stick to my recipe. If you're looking for a recipe that doesn't include making a mess by melting chocolate, then this is the recipe you're looking for. I suggest that people use the melted butter instead of oil,really good, also I didn't add the baking powder because I wanted the brownies to be chewy and fudgey, and it worked. So if you don't like dry cakey brownies I suggest leaving the baking powder out. I topped these with "creamy chocolate frosting" and melted the butter instead so the frosting would be fudgey and shiny, it worked out great!!! I will make these again, i think everyone should try this recipe.

text:
After dinner craving + cocoa powder= grateful I found this recipe.  20 min was perfect when using a 9x9 pan.  They came out thin, but dense and fudgy.  They were so easy to put together!  I whipped them up by hand- no mixer required!  Take the time to really whip the oil, eggs and sugar; and then fold in the dry ingredients. The only flaw was on my part, I added a bit too much vanilla and it overwhelmed the cocoa taste. I lined my pan with parchment and they were a since to take out of the pan.  My days of making bad brownies is over!

These were delicious- moist, rich, fudgey, with the classic slightly flaky top. I followed some other reviewers' suggestions: I used 1/4 C oil and 1/4C melted butter. I heated the oil, and with the hot melted butter, the sugar dissolved perfectly (no gritty texture). I also added a little more than 1/4C semi-sweet chocolate chips before transferring to the pan. The only reason I'm not rating 5 starts is that they do come out thin under one inch. Maybe this would be better with an 8X8 pan?

All in all pretty good recipe!

text:
I was skeptical because I've made brownies from a box all my life (thank you Betty Crocker!) but I didn't have a box mix and I needed a quick dessert.  Cookies just weren't in the picture.  So I decided to try this recipe.  Followed it for the most part but added about a teaspoon or so of finely ground coffee beans and about a quarter cup of Ghiradelli 60% coco chocolate chips.  Buttered the pan (8x8 glass pan), poured the batter in, and baked for about 27 minutes - still a little gooey in the middle, but pretty set up.  They look puffy when you first take them out of the oven, but then they settle to a pretty flat brownie - Not super cakey and not overly fudgy (my husband interprets that as undercooked).  I cut the pan into 12 brownies and my husband went back for seconds....twice.  Thus, I know this is a hit.  I thought they were plenty sweet and plenty chocolaty, but I suppose the chocolate chips might have helped that.  I will definitely make this again.

text:
These were good, but too cakey for my family. I made them with 1/2 butter and 1/2 canola oil.  The second time around, I adjusted the recipe as follows:
5tbsp butter, 3 tbsp canola oil, ADD a square (1 oz) of Baker's unsweet chocolate
I just heated those up and stirred until the chocolate melted into the butter/oil mixture (microwave).  I then added the sugar and stirred for a bit, then set it aside.  I mixed up the dry ingredients, then set that aside.  I went back to the slightly cooled sugar mixture and quickly beat in the eggs and vanilla, then quickly added the dry ingredients, then quickly poured it into the pan and baked it until a knife inserted about halfway between the middle and the edge came out with only a couple of crumbs.
The result was much more to our liking--fudgy with a bit of chew, especially around the edges.  Perfect.

text:
I don't usually rate a recipe unless it is outstanding, and this brownie recipe is awesome! It is easy to make and is as good if not better than other name brand fudge brownies. This recipe results in a chocolatey chewy brownie. I made it for the first time and doubled the batch and left it in the oven about 10 minutes longer than what the recipe called for. I used a 13" x 9" shiny baking pan and my double batch yielded 30 squares (about a two bite size slice). Your oven may require a different bake time, so I may have lucked out on my first try. Regardless, this recipe is a keeper, and I may never go back to brownie mixes again because these are that delectable!

I chose this recipe as it used oil, since I was out of butter. I doubled the recipe and followed it exactly. I did add about a half a bag of chocolate chips I wanted to use up. I baked in a 13 x 11 pan for 35 minutes.  I frosted with a peanut butter, cream cheese frosting.  The brownies were moist, chewy and came out about an inch or so thick.  They also had a nice crackly, shiny top that made me think twice about frosting them! Wonderful flavor that says BROWNIES!!!!! Gonna have some happy kids after school today! Will be making this recipe again.  (on a side note - I think the recipe is not going to work well, as written, using a small pan.  There is just not enough batter and the 25 minutes bake time would be too long.)

Wow! i printed this recipe out over 5 years ago and felt obligated to finally write a review.  these are simple, but AMAZING brownies.  so moist and fudgy.  i usually leave out the walnuts and always make with melted butter instead of oil.  these keep well for days.  i usually line the pan with lightly oiled foil to easily remove the brownies from the pan.  when the edges just start to pull away from the sides i take it out of the oven.  that way the edges crisp up a little, but don't get too hard.  these brownies are so easy and delicious.

text:
The first time I tried this recipe, my brownies stayed soft and raw WAY past the baking time. Finally I turned off the oven and let it dry. Then it got too hard. However, others liked its taste. I think I know the problem. HINT: if you sift the flour too much before measuring then you won't have enough flour and the ratio of liquid to solid will mess up and your brownies will take forever to bake. Instead, pack the flour when measuring, then sift it into the bowl. I measured the flour right the second time and that time my brownies were PERFECT! Fudgy, soft, and rich in taste. Will make again!

They are really chewy and fudy brownies! The thing I like best is that you don't need chocolate chips(I always run out when I feel like baking brownies =D)! Another thing is that all my experiences with brownie making have never turned out very well(some were too cakey some would bake they stayed watery, and some were just plain gross) but when i made this recipe, my whole family ate them right up and some of them don't like anything chocolatey but they really enjoyey this recipe! The reason I gave it 4 stars is that it needed a little kick of something... I don't really know what but I'm going to try it with some chocolate chips. You don't really get 16 pieces of the brownie and it fits in a 8x8 pan. Overall these brownies are great1 I am definatly going to use this recipe again!

These are the best brownies ever.  I always add some chocolate chips to my boxed brownies, so I did the same on this one, just 1/4 bag of semi-sweet choc chips. The only other thing I did, was double the recipe as others had said & placed it in a 9X13 pan & cooked for about 35 minutes on same degree!  YUMM!

I dont know.....Maybe I'm just so used to boxed brownies...(Betty Crocker in the red box is the best by far)......I've been trying to find a good "homemade" brownie recipe.  In this one, I used the butter option and I didnt put the baking powder in.  They came out about a millimeter thin...and fudgy....but theres something I've found in making brownies from scratch....they taste like either the flour or the cocoa powder is stale or something.  Maybe thats just the taste of not enough of the chocolate taste I crave.  Sorry folks, but I think I'll just stick to the box version.
